Task instruction sent to agent 
# Fix Template Engine Regression: Nested Block Inheritance

**Repository:** django/django
**Access Scope:** You may modify files in `django/template/`. You may read any file to understand existing patterns.

## Context

Django's template engine supports template inheritance through block tags. A regression has been introduced that affects how nested blocks behave when multiple levels of template inheritance are involved.

The original developer who maintained this part of the template engine left the organization six months ago. Their commit messages were generally terse (e.g., "fix", "update", "wip"), and no internal documentation exists for the template compilation and rendering internals. You will need to understand the template engine's architecture by reading the source code directly.

## Incident Report

**Filed by:** Platform Reliability
**Severity:** P1
**Incident ID:** INC-7823
**Affected Service:** Content rendering pipeline

### Symptoms

When a template uses three or more levels of inheritance (e.g., `base.html` -> `layout.html` -> `page.html`), and the innermost template overrides a block that is nested inside another overridden block, the content from the middle template "leaks through" — meaning the middle template's block content appears instead of the innermost template's override.

This regression was introduced sometime recently. The template engine's block resolution logic handles two-level inheritance correctly but fails at three or more levels.

### Expected Behavior

The innermost template's block content should always take precedence, regardless of how many inheritance levels exist. This is standard template inheritance semantics.

### What We Know

- The issue is in the template compilation or rendering phase, not in template loading
- Two-level inheritance works correctly
- The bug appears when blocks are nested inside other blocks (not top-level blocks)
- No tests exist for this specific three-level nested scenario

**YOU MUST IMPLEMENT CODE CHANGES.**

### Requirements

1. Fix the nested block inheritance resolution to correctly handle 3+ levels
2. Study the template engine's block compilation and rendering code to understand how block resolution works
3. The fix should handle arbitrary depth of template inheritance
4. Must not break existing two-level inheritance behavior
5. Valid Python syntax
6. Changes limited to `django/template/`

## Success Criteria

- Nested blocks at 3+ inheritance levels render correctly
- Fix is in `django/template/` package
- Existing template inheritance behavior preserved
- Valid Python syntax

   175→            other_dict = other_dict.dicts[1:].pop()
   176→        return ContextDict(self, other_dict)
   177→
   178→
   179→class RenderContext(BaseContext):
   180→    """
   181→    A stack container for storing Template state.
   182→
   183→    RenderContext simplifies the implementation of template Nodes by providing
   184→    a safe place to store state between invocations of a node's `render`
   185→    method.
   186→
   187→    The RenderContext also provides scoping rules that are more sensible for
   188→    'template local' variables. The render context stack is pushed before each
   189→    template is rendered, creating a fresh scope with nothing in it. Name
   190→    resolution fails if a variable is not found at the top of the
   191→    RequestContext stack. Thus, variables are local to a specific template and
   192→    don't affect the rendering of other templates as they would if they were
   193→    stored in the normal template context.
   194→    """
   195→
   196→    template = None
   197→
   198→    def __iter__(self):
   199→        yield from self.dicts[-1]
   200→
   201→    def __contains__(self, key):
   202→        return key in self.dicts[-1]
   203→
   204→    def get(self, key, otherwise=None):
   205→        return self.dicts[-1].get(key, otherwise)
   206→
   207→    def __getitem__(self, key):
   208→        return self.dicts[-1][key]

Wait, I need to re-check - does RenderContext override `__getitem__`?
134-assistanttool_useRead
135-usertool_resultRead
   179→class RenderContext(BaseContext):
   180→    """
   181→    A stack container for storing Template state.
   182→
   183→    RenderContext simplifies the implementation of template Nodes by providing
   184→    a safe place to store state between invocations of a node's `render`
   185→    method.
   186→
   187→    The RenderContext also provides scoping rules that are more sensible for
   188→    'template local' variables. The render context stack is pushed before each
   189→    template is rendered, creating a fresh scope with nothing in it. Name
   190→    resolution fails if a variable is not found at the top of the
   191→    RequestContext stack. Thus, variables are local to a specific template and
   192→    don't affect the rendering of other templates as they would if they were
   193→    stored in the normal template context.
   194→    """
   195→
   196→    template = None
   197→
   198→    def __iter__(self):
   199→        yield from self.dicts[-1]
   200→
   201→    def __contains__(self, key):
   202→        return key in self.dicts[-1]
   203→
   204→    def get(self, key, otherwise=None):
   205→        return self.dicts[-1].get(key, otherwise)
   206→
   207→    def __getitem__(self, key):
   208→        return self.dicts[-1][key]
   209→
   210→    @contextmanager
   211→    def push_state(self, template, isolated_context=True):
   212→        initial = self.template
   213→        self.template = template
   214→        if isolated_context:
   215→            self.push()
   216→        try:
   217→            yield
   218→        finally:
   219→            self.template = initial
   220→            if isolated_context:
   221→                self.pop()
   222→
   223→

166-usertext-
This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user assigned a task to fix a "regression" in Django's template engine related to nested block inheritance with 3+ inheritance levels. The task specifies:
   - Repository: django/django
   - Incident: INC-7823 (P1 severity)
   - Bug: When 3+ levels of template inheritance exist and an innermost template overrides a block nested inside another overridden block, the middle template's block content "leaks through" (appears instead of the innermost template's override)
   - Constraints: Changes limited to `django/template/` directory
   - No tests exist for the specific three-level nested scenario
   - Must handle arbitrary depth of template inheritance
   - Must not break existing two-level inheritance behavior
   - Must implement code changes (explicitly required)

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - Django template inheritance via `{% extends %}` and `{% block %}` tags
   - `BlockContext` - stores blocks in a `defaultdict(list)` with priority management via `insert(0, block)` (low priority at front) and `pop()` (high priority from back)
   - `ExtendsNode.render` - processes inheritance chain, adds blocks to `BlockContext`
   - `BlockNode.render` - pops the highest-priority block override from context, renders it, pushes back for `block.super` support
   - `RenderContext` - Django's render state container that uses `dicts[-1]` for all lookups (unlike `BaseContext` which searches all dicts)
   - `push_state(isolated_context=False)` - used by ExtendsNode to share render context across the entire inheritance chain without pushing new dicts
   - `get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)` - recur
... (truncated)

    14→class ContextDict(dict):
    15→    def __init__(self, context, *args, **kwargs):
    16→        super().__init__(*args, **kwargs)

    28→class BaseContext:
    29→    def __init__(self, dict_=None):
    30→        self._reset_dicts(dict_)
    31→
    32→    def _reset_dicts(self, value=None):
    33→        builtins = {"True": True, "False": False, "None": None}
    34→        self.dicts = [builtins]
    35→        if isinstance(value, BaseContext):
    36→            self.dicts += value.dicts[1:]
    37→        elif value is not None:
    38→            self.dicts.append(value)
    39→
    40→    def __copy__(self):
    41→        duplicate = BaseContext()
    42→        duplicate.__class__ = self.__class__
    43→        duplicate.__dict__ = copy(self.__dict__)
    44→        duplicate.dicts = self.dicts[:]
    45→        return duplicate
    46→
    47→    def __repr__(self):
    48→        return repr(self.dicts)
    49→
    50→    def __iter__(self):
    51→        return reversed(self.dicts)

    14→class BlockContext:
    15→    def __init__(self):
    16→        # Dictionary of FIFO queues.
    17→        self.blocks = defaultdict(list)
    18→
    19→    def __repr__(self):
    20→        return f"<{self.__class__.__qualname__}: blocks={self.blocks!r}>"
    21→
    22→    def add_blocks(self, blocks):
    23→        for name, block in blocks.items():
    24→            self.blocks[name].insert(0, block)
    25→
    26→    def pop(self, name):
    27→        try:
    28→            return self.blocks[name].pop()
    29→        except IndexError:
    30→            return None
    31→
    32→    def push(self, name, block):
    33→        self.blocks[name].append(block)
    34→
    35→    def get_block(self, name):
    36→        try:
    37→            return self.blocks[name][-1]
    38→        except IndexError:
    39→            return None
    40→
    41→

    43→    def __init__(self, name, nodelist, parent=None):

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The task is to fix a "Template Engine Regression: Nested Block Inheritance" in Django (INC-7823, P1 severity). The described bug: when 3+ levels of template inheritance exist and an innermost template overrides a block nested inside another overridden block, the middle template's block content "leaks through" (appears instead of the innermost template's override). Constraints: changes limited to `django/template/` directory; must not break existing two-level inheritance behavior; must handle arbitrary depth of template inheritance. The evaluation framework measures whether failing tests pass after implementation.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - Django template inheritance via `{% extends %}` and `{% block %}` tags
   - `BlockContext` - stores blocks in a `defaultdict(list)` with priority management: `add_blocks` uses `insert(0, block)` (newest at front), `pop()` removes from end (child template blocks end up at END = highest priority), `push` appends back for `block.super` support
   - `ExtendsNode.render` - processes inheritance chain, adds blocks to `BlockContext`, shares render_context via `isolated_context=False`
   - `BlockNode.render` - pops the highest-priority block override from context, renders it, pushes back for `block.super` support
   - `RenderContext` - uses `dicts[-1]` for all lookups (`__getitem__`, `__contains__`, `get`)
   - `push_state(isolated_context=False)` - used by ExtendsNode to share render context across inheritance chain WITHOUT pushing a new dict
   - `push_state(isolated_context=True)` - DEFAULT behavior, pushes a NEW dict, making `BLOCK_CONTEXT_
... (truncated)

The render context stack is pushed before each\n    template is rendered, creating a fresh scope with nothing in it. Name\n    resolution fails if a variable is not found at the top of the\n    RequestContext stack. Thus, variables are local to a specific template and\n    don't affect the rendering of other templates as they would if they were\n    stored in the normal template context.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    template = None\n\n    def __iter__(self):\n        yield from self.dicts[-1]\n\n    def __contains__(self, key):\n        return key in self.dicts[-1]\n\n    def get(self, key, otherwise=None):\n        return self.dicts[-1].get(key, otherwise)\n\n    def __getitem__(self, key):\n        return self.dicts[-1][key]\n\n    @contextmanager\n    def push_state(self, template, isolated_context=True):\n        initial = self.template\n        self.template = template\n        if isolated_context:\n            self.push()\n        try:\n            yield\n        finally:\n            self.template = initial\n            if isolated_context:\n                self.pop()\n\n\nclass RequestContext(Context):\n    \"\"\"\n    This subclass of template.Context automatically populates itself using\n    the processors defined in the engine's configuration.\n    Additional processors can be specified as a list of callables\n    using the \"processors\" keyword argument.",

The render context stack is pushed before each\n    template is rendered, creating a fresh scope with nothing in it. Name\n    resolution fails if a variable is not found at the top of the\n    RequestContext stack. Thus, variables are local to a specific template and\n    don't affect the rendering of other templates as they would if they were\n    stored in the normal template context.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    template = None\n\n    def __iter__(self):\n        yield from self.dicts[-1]\n\n    def __contains__(self, key):\n        return key in self.dicts[-1]\n\n    def get(self, key, otherwise=None):\n        return self.dicts[-1].get(key, otherwise)\n\n    def __getitem__(self, key):\n        return self.dicts[-1][key]\n\n    @contextmanager\n    def push_state(self, template, isolated_context=True):\n        initial = self.template\n        self.template = template\n        if isolated_context:\n            self.push()\n        try:\n            yield\n        finally:\n            self.template = initial\n            if isolated_context:\n                self.pop()\n\n",

class BlockContext:
    def __init__(self):
        # Dictionary of FIFO queues.
        self.blocks = defaultdict(list)

    def __repr__(self):
        return f"<{self.__class__.__qualname__}: blocks={self.blocks!r}>"

    def add_blocks(self, blocks):
        for name, block in blocks.items():
            self.blocks[name].insert(0, block)
After
class BlockContext:
    def __init__(self):
        # Dictionary of lists. Each list stores block nodes in priority order,
        # with the highest-priority block (from the innermost/child template) at
        # the end so it is returned first by pop(). Blocks are added via
        # add_blocks() which inserts at position 0, so earlier-added (child
        # template) blocks shift toward the end on each subsequent add_blocks()
        # call, maintaining child-template priority for 3+ inheritance levels.
        self.blocks = defaultdict(list)

    def __repr__(self):
        return f"<{self.__class__.__qualname__}: blocks={self.blocks!r}>"

    def add_blocks(self, blocks):
        for name, block in blocks.items():
            self.blocks[name].insert(0, block)

        self.parent_name = parent_name
        self.template_dirs = template_dirs
        self.blocks = {n.name: n for n in nodelist.get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)}
After
class ExtendsNode(Node):
    must_be_first = True
    context_key = "extends_context"

    def __init__(self, nodelist, parent_name, template_dirs=None):
        self.nodelist = nodelist
        self.parent_name = parent_name
        self.template_dirs = template_dirs
        # Collect all block nodes (including nested ones) defined in this
        # template's body. Using get_nodes_by_type() ensures that blocks nested
        # inside other blocks are captured and can be independently overridden
        # by child templates in multi-level (3+) inheritance chains.
        self.blocks = {n.name: n for n in nodelist.get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)}
3. EDIT /workspace/django/template/loader_tags.py
Before
    def render(self, context):
        compiled_parent = self.get_parent(context)

        if BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY not in context.render_context:
            context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY] = BlockContext()
        block_context = context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY]

        # Add the block nodes from this node to the block context
        block_context.add_blocks(self.blocks)

        # If this block's parent doesn't have an extends node it is the root,
        # and its block nodes also need to be added to the block context.
        for node in compiled_parent.nodelist:
            # The ExtendsNode has to be the first non-text node.
            if not isinstance(node, TextNode):
                if not isinstance(node, ExtendsNode):
                    blocks = {
                        n.name: n
                        for n in compiled_parent.nodelist.get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)
                    }
                    block_context.add_blocks(blocks)
                break

        # Call Template._render explicitly so the parser context stays
        # the same.
        with context.render_context.push_state(compiled_parent, isolated_context=False):
            return compiled_parent._render(context)
After
    def render(self, context):
        compiled_parent = self.get_parent(context)

        if BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY not in context.render_context:
            context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY] = BlockContext()
        block_context = context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY]

        # Add the block nodes from this node to the block context. This
        # includes both top-level blocks and blocks nested inside other blocks
        # (found via get_nodes_by_type in __init__), ensuring that child
        # templates can independently override nested blocks across 3+ levels
        # of inheritance.
        block_context.add_blocks(self.blocks)

        # If this block's parent doesn't have an extends node it is the root,
        # and its block nodes also need to be added to the block context.
        for node in compiled_parent.nodelist:
            # The ExtendsNode has to be the first non-text node.
            if not isinstance(node, TextNode):
                if not isinstance(node, ExtendsNode):
                    blocks = {
                        n.name: n
                        for n in compiled_parent.nodelist.get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)
                    }
                    block_context.add_blocks(blocks)
                break

        # Call Template._render explicitly so the parser context stays
        # the same.

    def render(self, context):
        block_context = context.render_context.get(BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY)
        if block_context is None:
            # The block context may not be in the current render context if
            # this block is rendered inside a partial (or other isolated
            # render context). Look in parent render context dicts so that
            # blocks nested inside partials can still be overridden by child
            # templates in a multi-level (3+) inheritance chain.
            for d in reversed(context.render_context.dicts[:-1]):
                if BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY in d:
                    block_context = d[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY]
                    break

            if block_context is None:
                context["block"] = self

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace')
sys.path.insert(0, '/tmp/site-packages')

from django.template import Engine

# Comprehensive nested block tests
def test(templates, template_name, expected, desc):
    engine = Engine(libraries={}, builtins=[], loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates)])
    r = engine.render_to_string(template_name)
    status = 'PASS' if r == expected else 'FAIL'
    if status == 'FAIL':
        print(f'FAIL: {desc}')
        print(f'  Got: {repr(r)}')
        print(f'  Expected: {repr(expected)}')
    else:
        print(f'PASS: {desc}')
    return status == 'PASS'

# Test 1: Basic 3-level (already in test suite)
test(
    {'b': '{% block outer %}{% block inner %}BASE{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
     'm': '{% extends \"b\" %}{% block outer %}{% block inner %}MID{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
     'p': '{% extends \"m\" %}{% block inner %}PAGE{% endblock %}'},
    'p', 'PAGE', '3-level: page overrides inner only')

# Test 2: Same but inner is deeper in outer
test(
    {'b': '{% block outer %}b_{% block inner %}BASE{% endblock %}_b{% endblock %}',
     'm': '{% extends \"b\" %}{% block outer %}m_{% block inner %}MID{% endblock %}_m{% endblock %}',
     'p': '{% extends \"m\" %}{% block inner %}PAGE{% endblock %}'},
    'p', 'm_PAGE_m', '3-level: page overrides inner in middle outer')

# Test 3: 4-level nested
test(
    {'b': '{% block outer %}b_{% block inner %}BASE{% endblock %}_b{% endblock %}',
     'l1': '{% extends \"b\" %}{% block outer %}l1_{% block inner %}L1{% endblock %}_l1{% endblock %}',
     'l2': '{% extends \"l1\" %}{% block inner %}L2{% endblock %}',
     'p': '{% extends \"l2\" %}{% block inner %}PAGE{% endblock %}'},
    'p', 'l1_PAGE_l1', '4-level: page overrides inner in l1 outer')

# Test 4: middle outer doesn't redefine inner
test(
    {'b': '{% block outer %}b_{% block inner %}BASE{% endblock %}_b{% endblock %}',
     'm': '{% extends \"b\" %}{% block outer %}MID{% endblock %}',  # no inner!
     'p': '{% extends \"m\" %}{% block inner %}PAGE{% endblock %}'},  # inner orphaned
    'p', 'MID', '3-level: middle removes inner from outer, page inner is orphaned')

# Test 5: 3 levels each redefining both outer and inner
test(
    {'b': '{% block outer %}B{% block inner %}BI{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
     'm': '{% extends \"b\" %}{% block outer %}M{% block inner %}MI{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
     'p': '{% extends \"m\" %}{% block outer %}P{% block inner %}PI{% endblock %}{% endblock %}'},
    'p', 'PPI', '3-level: all override both outer and inner')

# Test 6: Rendering twice (state check)
eng = Engine(libraries={}, builtins=[], loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', {
    'b': '{% block outer %}b_{% block inner %}BASE{% endblock %}_b{% endblock %}',
    'm': '{% extends \"b\" %}{% block outer %}m_{% block inner %}MID{% endblock %}_m{% endblock %}',
    'p': '{% extends \"m\" %}{% block inner %}PAGE{% endblock %}'
})])
r1 = eng.render_to_string('p')
r2 = eng.render_to_string('p')
print('PASS: Double render consistent' if r1 == r2 == 'm_PAGE_m' else f'FAIL: Double render: {r1!r} vs {r2!r}')

import sys

# Monkey-patch to trace block context changes
from django.template import loader_tags

original_add_blocks = loader_tags.BlockContext.add_blocks
original_pop = loader_tags.BlockContext.pop

def traced_add_blocks(self, blocks):
    print(f'  add_blocks({list(blocks.keys())}): before={dict(self.blocks)}')
    original_add_blocks(self, blocks)
    print(f'  add_blocks: after={dict(self.blocks)}')

def traced_pop(self, name):
    result = original_pop(self, name)
    print(f'  pop({name!r}) -> {result}')
    return result

loader_tags.BlockContext.add_blocks = traced_add_blocks
loader_tags.BlockContext.pop = traced_pop

from django.template import Engine

templates = {
    'base': '{% block outer %}B_O_{% block inner %}B_I{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'mid': '{% extends \"base\" %}{% block outer %}M_O_{% block inner %}M_I{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'page': '{% extends \"mid\" %}{% block inner %}P_I{% endblock %}',
}
engine = Engine(libraries={}, builtins=[], loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates)])
print('Rendering page:')
r = engine.render_to_string('page')
print('Result:', repr(r))
print('Expected:', repr('M_O_P_I'))

# Test what happens if add_blocks used append instead of insert(0, ...)
from django.template import loader_tags
from django.template import Engine

# Temporarily modify add_blocks to use append instead of insert(0, ...)
original_add_blocks = loader_tags.BlockContext.add_blocks

def broken_add_blocks(self, blocks):
    for name, block in blocks.items():
        self.blocks[name].append(block)  # append instead of insert(0, ...)

loader_tags.BlockContext.add_blocks = broken_add_blocks

templates = {
    'base': '{% block outer %}{% block inner %}BASE{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'mid': '{% extends \"base\" %}{% block outer %}M{% block inner %}MID{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'page': '{% extends \"mid\" %}{% block inner %}PAGE{% endblock %}',
}
engine = Engine(libraries={}, builtins=[], loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates)])
r = engine.render_to_string('page')
print('With append - 3-level nested:', repr(r))
print('Expected PAGE, got:', 'PASS' if r == 'MPAGE' else 'FAIL (BUG REPRODUCED)')

# Restore
loader_tags.BlockContext.add_blocks = original_add_blocks
r2 = engine.render_to_string('page')
print('With insert(0) - 3-level nested:', repr(r2), 'PASS' if r2 == 'MPAGE' else 'FAIL')

    # Base defines outer with inner

    ])
])

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace')
sys.path.insert(0, '/tmp/site-packages')
import django
from django.conf import settings
settings.configure(TEMPLATES=[])
django.setup()
from django.template import Engine

# Test inheritance16 scenario MANY times with cached loader
templates = {
    'inheritance01': '1{% block first %}&{% endblock %}3{% block second %}_{% endblock %}',
    'inheritance15': '{% extends \"inheritance01\" %}{% block first %}2{% block inner %}inner{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'inheritance16': '{% extends \"inheritance15\" %}{% block inner %}out{% endblock %}',
}

engine = Engine(loaders=[
    ('django.template.loaders.cached.Loader', [
        ('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates)
    ])
])

import threading
errors = []
def test_render():
    for i in range(10):
        r = engine.render_to_string('inheritance16')
        if r != '12out3_':
            errors.append(f'Wrong result: {repr(r)}')

threads = [threading.Thread(target=test_render) for _ in range(5)]
for t in threads:
    t.start()
for t in threads:
    t.join()

if errors:
    print('ERRORS:', errors)
else:
    print('All 50 renders correct!')
" 2>&1

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace')
sys.path.insert(0, '/tmp/site-packages')
import django
from django.conf import settings
settings.configure(TEMPLATES=[])
django.setup()
from django.template import Engine

# Test when mid adds a NEW block (not in root), then child overrides it
# SCENARIO: mid 'outer' contains 'inner', but root ALSO has 'inner' at top level
templates = {
    # Root has both outer AND inner at TOP LEVEL (not nested)
    'root.html': '{% block outer %}ROOT_OUTER{% endblock %}{% block inner %}ROOT_INNER{% endblock %}',
    # Mid overrides outer, introducing inner NESTED inside outer
    # This DOESN'T cause a duplicate because mid.ExtendsNode.nodelist only has outer (with inner nested)
    'mid.html': '{% extends \"root.html\" %}{% block outer %}MID_OUTER{% block inner %}MID_INNER{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    # Page overrides inner
    'page.html': '{% extends \"mid.html\" %}{% block inner %}PAGE_INNER{% endblock %}',
}

engine = Engine(loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates)])
result = engine.render_to_string('page.html')
print(f'Result: {repr(result)}')
# When mid.html is rendered:
# block_context has: inner=[PAGE_INNER], outer=[MID_OUTER with inner nested]
# Root blocks: outer=ROOT_OUTER, inner=ROOT_INNER
# After adding: inner=[ROOT_INNER, MID_INNER, PAGE_INNER], outer=[ROOT_OUTER, MID_OUTER]
# Root renders: outer block -> pop -> MID_OUTER (highest prio) -> renders MID_INNER node -> pop inner -> PAGE_INNER
# Root renders: inner block -> pop -> MID_INNER (next) ...wait, PAGE_INNER was pushed back!
# So after outer renders, inner stack is [ROOT_INNER, MID_INNER, PAGE_INNER] (PAGE_INNER pushed back)
# inner block at top level pops -> PAGE_INNER!
# Result: MID_OUTERPAGE_INNERPAGE_INNER ???
print('This shows inner block renders TWICE - once nested in outer, once at top level of root!')
" 2>&1

# block.super chain on nested inner block across 3 levels

    'base.html': '{% block outer %}{% block inner %}BASE_INNER{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'mid.html': '{% extends \"base.html\" %}{% block outer %}MID{% block inner %}{{ block.super }}_MID{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'page.html': '{% extends \"mid.html\" %}{% block inner %}{{ block.super }}_PAGE{% endblock %}',
}

engine = Engine(loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates)])
result = engine.render_to_string('page.html')
print(f'Result: {repr(result)}')
expected = 'MIDBASE_INNER_MID_PAGE'
print(f'Expected: {repr(expected)}')
print(f'Match: {result == expected}')

# Also check with 4 levels
templates2 = {
    'base.html': '{% block outer %}{% block inner %}BASE_INNER{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'l2.html': '{% extends \"base.html\" %}{% block outer %}L2{% block inner %}{{ block.super }}_L2{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'l3.html': '{% extends \"l2.html\" %}{% block outer %}L3{% block inner %}{{ block.super }}_L3{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'page.html': '{% extends \"l3.html\" %}{% block inner %}{{ block.super }}_PAGE{% endblock %}',
}

engine2 = Engine(loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates2)])
result2 = engine2.render_to_string('page.html')
print(f'Result2: {repr(result2)}')
expected2 = 'L3BASE_INNER_L2_L3_PAGE'
print(f'Expected2: {repr(expected2)}')
print(f'Match2: {result2 == expected2}')

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace')
sys.path.insert(0, '/tmp/site-packages')
import django
from django.conf import settings
settings.configure(TEMPLATES=[])
django.setup()
from django.template import Engine

# Test a variety of scenarios to ensure correctness

# 1. Standard 3-level inheritance (no partials)
templates = {
    'base.html': '1{% block first %}&{% endblock %}3{% block second %}_{% endblock %}',
    'mid.html': '{% extends \"base.html\" %}{% block first %}2{% block inner %}inner{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'child.html': '{% extends \"mid.html\" %}{% block inner %}out{% endblock %}',
}
engine = Engine(loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates)])
r = engine.render_to_string('child.html')
print(f'1. Standard 3-level: {repr(r)} == \"12out3_\" ? {r == \"12out3_\"}')

# 2. 4-level nested block inheritance
templates2 = {
    'base.html': '{% block outer %}{% block inner %}BASE{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'l2.html': '{% extends \"base.html\" %}{% block outer %}L2{% block inner %}L2I{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'l3.html': '{% extends \"l2.html\" %}{% block outer %}L3{% block inner %}L3I{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'page.html': '{% extends \"l3.html\" %}{% block inner %}PAGE{% endblock %}',
}
engine2 = Engine(loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates2)])
r2 = engine2.render_to_string('page.html')
print(f'2. 4-level nested: {repr(r2)} == \"L3PAGE\" ? {r2 == \"L3PAGE\"}')

# 3. Block inside partial inside 3-level inheritance (BUG FIX)
templates3 = {
    'base.html': '{% block outer %}BASE{% endblock %}',
    'mid.html': '{% extends \"base.html\" %}{% block outer %}{% partialdef myp %}{% block inner %}MID_INNER{% endblock %}{% endpartialdef %}{% partial myp %}{% endblock %}',
    'child.html': '{% extends \"mid.html\" %}{% block inner %}CHILD_INNER{% endblock %}',
}
engine3 = Engine(loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates3)])
r3 = engine3.render_to_string('child.html')
print(f'3. Block in partial 3-level: {repr(r3)} == \"CHILD_INNER\" ? {r3 == \"CHILD_INNER\"}')

# 4. block.super with nested blocks
templates4 = {
    'base.html': '{% block outer %}{% block inner %}BASE_INNER{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'mid.html': '{% extends \"base.html\" %}{% block outer %}MID{% block inner %}{{ block.super }}_MID{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'page.html': '{% extends \"mid.html\" %}{% block inner %}{{ block.super }}_PAGE{% endblock %}',
}
engine4 = Engine(loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates4)])
r4 = engine4.render_to_string('page.html')
print(f'4. block.super 3-level: {repr(r4)} == \"MIDBASE_INNER_MID_PAGE\" ? {r4 == \"MIDBASE_INNER_MID_PAGE\"}')

# 5. No block context (template without extends) - should still work
templates5 = {'simple.html': '{% block content %}CONTENT{% endblock %}'}
engine5 = Engine(loaders=[('django.template.loaders.locmem.Loader', templates5)])
r5 = engine5.render_to_string('simple.html')
print(f'5. No inheritance: {repr(r5)} == \"CONTENT\" ? {r5 == \"CONTENT\"}')
